<th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><a href="/wiki/Video_game_genre" title="Video game genre">Genre(s)</a></th>
<td style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Survival_horror" title="Survival horror">Survival horror</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Mode(s)</th>
<td style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Single-player_video_game" title="Single-player video game">Single-player</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i><b>Resident Evil 4</b></i>, known in Japan as <i><b>Biohazard 4</b></i> (<a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>: バイオハザード４ <a href="/wiki/Hepburn_romanization" title="Hepburn romanization">Hepburn</a>: <i>Baiohazādo Fō</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Survival_horror" title="Survival horror">survival horror</a> video game developed and published by <a href="/wiki/Capcom" title="Capcom">Capcom</a>. The sixth major installment in the <i><a href="/wiki/Resident_Evil" title="Resident Evil">Resident Evil</a></i> series, the game was originally released for the <a href="/wiki/GameCube" title="GameCube">GameCube</a> in North America and Japan in January 2005, and in Europe and Australia in March 2005. The story of <i>Resident Evil 4</i> follows the U.S. government special agent <a href="/wiki/Leon_S._Kennedy" title="Leon S. Kennedy">Leon S. Kennedy</a>, who is sent on a mission to rescue Ashley Graham, the U.S. President's daughter whom a sinister cult has kidnapped. Traveling to a rural area of Spain, Leon fights hordes of violent villagers and reunites with the mysterious spy <a href="/wiki/Ada_Wong" title="Ada Wong">Ada Wong</a>.</p>
<p>First hinted at in December 1999, <i>Resident Evil 4</i> underwent a long development time during which four proposed versions of the game were discarded. Initially developed for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a>, the first attempt was directed by <a href="/wiki/Hideki_Kamiya" title="Hideki Kamiya">Hideki Kamiya</a> after producer Shinji Mikami requested him to create a new entry in the <i>Resident Evil</i> series. Nevertheless, it was decided to start development over again. The game was intended to be a GameCube exclusive as part of the <a href="/wiki/Capcom_Five" title="Capcom Five">Capcom Five</a>, but a PlayStation 2 version was announced before the game was released for the GameCube. <i>Resident Evil 4</i> was subsequently released for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>, and in downsized versions for <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zeebo" title="Zeebo">Zeebo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> (exclusive to <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Electronics" title="Samsung Electronics">Samsung</a> devices outside of Japan).</p>
<p><i>Resident Evil 4</i> garnered critical acclaim. It received multiple <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_of_the_Year" title="Game of the Year">Game of the Year</a> awards for <a href="/wiki/2005_in_video_gaming" title="2005 in video gaming">2005</a> and was seen as a successful <a href="/wiki/Cross-platform" title="Cross-platform">cross-platform</a> hit that influenced the evolution of the survival horror and <a href="/wiki/Third-person_shooter" title="Third-person shooter">third-person shooter</a> genres. The game pioneered and popularized the "over the shoulder" <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third-person_view" title="Third-person view">third-person view</a> perspective in video games. It has since been widely considered <a href="/wiki/List_of_video_games_considered_the_best" title="List of video games considered the best">to be one of the best video games of all time</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gameplay">Gameplay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_Evil_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Gameplay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The player controls the protagonist <a href="/wiki/Leon_S._Kennedy" title="Leon S. Kennedy">Leon S. Kennedy</a> from a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third-person_view" title="Third-person view">third-person</a> perspective. The gameplay focuses on action and shootouts involving crowds of enemies in large open areas. The camera is placed behind Leon and zooms in for an over-the-shoulder view when aiming a weapon, or a first-person view when aiming with a sniper rifle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> There is no crosshair for firearms, instead, every firearm has a laser sight. Unlike previous games where players can only shoot straight, up or down, players have more options. For example, shots to the feet can cause enemies to stumble, shots to the arms can make them drop their weapons, and headshots instantly kill most human enemies. Players can shoot down projectiles like thrown axes or scythes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laser_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-laser-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Resident_Evil_4_Ganado_village.png"><img alt="An image of a young man defending himself against a horde of humanoid enemies in a village setting. The camera is behind the man's shoulder, placing him in the bottom left corner and the attackers in the background of the picture." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="286" data-file-width="512" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Resident_Evil_4_Ganado_village.png/220px-Resident_Evil_4_Ganado_village.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Resident_Evil_4_Ganado_village.png/330px-Resident_Evil_4_Ganado_village.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Resident_Evil_4_Ganado_village.png/440px-Resident_Evil_4_Ganado_village.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Resident_Evil_4_Ganado_village.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Leon in battle with a group of Ganados. Unlike previous entries in the series, <i>Resident Evil 4</i> has the camera following directly behind the main character. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laser_sight" title="Laser sight">laser sight</a> enables the player to target key hit zones on enemies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laser_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-laser-5">[5]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Another aspect of <i>Resident Evil 4</i>, new to the series, is the inclusion of context-sensitive controls. Based on the situation, players can interact with the environment: kicking down a ladder, jumping out of a window, dodging an attack or executing a "finishing move" on weakened enemies. There are also <a href="/wiki/Quick_time_event" title="Quick time event">quick time events</a>, in which the player must press buttons indicated on-screen to execute actions such as dodging a falling boulder or wrestling an enemy to stay alive. These are often incorporated into the game's many <a href="/wiki/Boss_(video_gaming)" title="Boss (video gaming)">boss</a> fights, where the player must avoid instant kill attacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The main enemies are violent villagers referred to as <i>Los Ganados</i> ("The Cattle" in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>). <i>Los Ganados</i> can dodge, wield melee and projectile weapons, and are capable of working collectively and communicating with each other. They were once simple farmers until becoming the product of an infestation of <i>Las Plagas</i> ("The <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Plague" title="wiktionary:Plague">Plague</a>" in Spanish).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The inventory system of the game features a grid system, represented by an <a href="/wiki/Briefcase" title="Briefcase">attaché case</a>, that has each item take up a certain number of spaces. The case can be upgraded several times, allowing for more space. Weapons, ammunition, and healing items are kept in the case, while key items and treasures are kept in a separate menu. Items may be bought from and sold to a merchant that appears in various locations throughout the game. He sells first aid sprays, weapons, allows for weapons to be upgraded and buys various treasures that Leon finds. The various weapons each have their own advantages and disadvantages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Capcom added new content made specifically for the PlayStation 2 version of the game, which was later incorporated into the PC and Wii releases. The largest addition is "Separate Ways", a <a href="/wiki/Minigame" title="Minigame">minigame</a> which focuses on <a href="/wiki/Ada_Wong" title="Ada Wong">Ada Wong</a>'s involvement in <i>Resident Evil 4</i> and her connection to the series' villain <a href="/wiki/Albert_Wesker" title="Albert Wesker">Albert Wesker</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> "Ada's Report", a five-part documentary, analyzes Ada's relationship with Wesker and his role in the plot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Other <a href="/wiki/Unlockable_(gaming)" title="Unlockable (gaming)">unlockable</a> content in all versions includes the minigames "The Mercenaries" and "Assignment Ada" (using Ada to retrieve <i>Las Plagas</i> samples), new costumes for Leon and Ashley, new weapons, and a <a href="/wiki/Cutscene" title="Cutscene">cutscene</a> browser.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_Evil_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Six years after the events of <i><a href="/wiki/Resident_Evil_2" title="Resident Evil 2">Resident Evil 2</a></i>, former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raccoon_City" title="Raccoon City">Raccoon City</a> police officer <a href="/wiki/Leon_S._Kennedy" title="Leon S. Kennedy">Leon S. Kennedy</a> (<a href="/wiki/Paul_Mercier_(actor)" title="Paul Mercier (actor)">Paul Mercier</a>) is sent on a mission to rescue <a href="/wiki/List_of_Resident_Evil_characters#Ashley_Graham" title="List of Resident Evil characters">Ashley Graham</a> (<a href="/wiki/Carolyn_Lawrence" title="Carolyn Lawrence">Carolyn Lawrence</a>), the U.S. President's daughter, who has been kidnapped by a mysterious cult.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> He travels to a nameless rural village in an unspecified part of Spain, where he encounters a group of hostile villagers who pledge their lives to <i>Los Illuminados</i> ("The Enlightened Ones" in Spanish), the cult that kidnapped Ashley.</p>
<p>While in the village, Leon is captured by its chief, Bitores Mendez, and injected with a mind-controlling <a href="/wiki/Parasitism" title="Parasitism">parasite</a> known as <i>Las Plagas</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plagas_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-plagas-14">[14]</a></sup> He finds himself held captive with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luis_Sera" title="Luis Sera">Luis Sera</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rino_Romano" title="Rino Romano">Rino Romano</a>), a former <i>Los Illuminados</i> researcher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The two work together to escape, but then quickly go their separate ways. Leon discovers that Ashley is being held in a church, and rescues her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> They both escape from the church after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Osmund_Saddler" title="Osmund Saddler">Osmund Saddler</a> (<a href="/wiki/Michael_Gough_(voice_actor)" title="Michael Gough (voice actor)">Michael Gough</a>), leader of the <i>Illuminados</i>, reveals his plan to use the plaga they injected into Ashley to manipulate her into injecting the president of the United States with the "sample" (a Master Plaga) once she returns home, allowing Saddler to begin his conquest of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> After killing Mendez, Leon and Ashley try to take refuge in a castle but are attacked by more <i>Illuminados</i> under the command of Ramon Salazar (Rene Mujica), another of Saddler's henchmen who own the castle,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plagas_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-plagas-14">[14]</a></sup> and the two become separated by Salazar's traps. Meanwhile, Luis searches for the pills to slow Leon and Ashley's infection, as well as a sample of <i>Las Plagas</i>. He brings the two items to Leon but is killed by Saddler, who takes the sample, while the pills to suppress the infection remain in Leon's hands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> While in the castle, Leon briefly encounters <a href="/wiki/Ada_Wong" title="Ada Wong">Ada Wong</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sally_Cahill" title="Sally Cahill">Sally Cahill</a>), a woman from his past who supports him during his mission. He then battles his way through the castle before finally killing Salazar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Afterward, Leon travels to a nearby island research facility, where he continues the search for Ashley. He soon discovers that one of his former training comrades, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jack_Krauser" title="Jack Krauser">Jack Krauser</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jim_Ward_(voice_actor)" title="Jim Ward (voice actor)">Jim Ward</a>), who was believed to have been killed in a helicopter crash two years prior, is responsible for her kidnapping.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> It is eventually revealed that both Ada and Krauser are working with <a href="/wiki/Albert_Wesker" title="Albert Wesker">Albert Wesker</a> (<a href="/wiki/Richard_Waugh_(actor)" title="Richard Waugh (actor)">Richard Waugh</a>), for whom both intend to secure a <i>Plagas</i> sample.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Suspicious of the mercenary's intentions, Saddler orders Krauser to kill Leon, believing that no matter which one dies, he will benefit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> After Krauser's defeat, Leon rescues Ashley, and they remove the <i>Plagas</i> from their bodies using a specialized <a href="/wiki/Radiation_therapy" title="Radiation therapy">radiotherapeutic</a> device. Leon finally confronts Saddler, and with Ada's help, manages to kill him. However, Ada takes the sample from Leon at gunpoint before escaping in a helicopter,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> leaving Leon and Ashley to escape via her jet-ski as the island self-destructs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_Evil_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scrapped_versions">Scrapped versions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_Evil_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Scrapped versions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>First hinted at in early December 1999,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> <i>Resident Evil 4</i> underwent a lengthy development time during which at least four proposed versions of the game were discarded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egm2005_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-egm2005-26">[26]</a></sup> Initially developed for the PlayStation 2, the first attempt was directed by <a href="/wiki/Hideki_Kamiya" title="Hideki Kamiya">Hideki Kamiya</a> after producer <a href="/wiki/Shinji_Mikami" title="Shinji Mikami">Shinji Mikami</a> requested him to create a new entry in the <i>Resident Evil</i> series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dmcbegin_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-dmcbegin-27">[27]</a></sup> Around the turn of the millennium,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dmcscenario_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-dmcscenario-28">[28]</a></sup> <i>Resident Evil 2</i> writer <a href="/wiki/Noboru_Sugimura" title="Noboru Sugimura">Noboru Sugimura</a> created a scenario for the title,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> based on Kamiya's idea to make a "cool" and "stylish" <a href="/wiki/Action_game" title="Action game">action game</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The story was based on unraveling the mystery surrounding the body of protagonist Tony,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> an invincible man with skills and an intellect exceeding that of normal people, with his superhuman abilities explained with biotechnology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dmcscenario_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-dmcscenario-28">[28]</a></sup> As Kamiya felt the playable character did not look brave and heroic enough in battles from a fixed angle, he decided to drop the prerendered backgrounds from previous installments and instead opted for a <a href="/wiki/Virtual_camera_system" title="Virtual camera system">dynamic camera system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dmcbegin_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-dmcbegin-27">[27]</a></sup> This new direction required the team to make a trip to Europe, where they spent 11 days in the United Kingdom and Spain, photographing things like <a href="/wiki/Gothic_art" title="Gothic art">Gothic</a> statues, bricks, and stone pavements for use in <a href="/wiki/Texture_mapping" title="Texture mapping">textures</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Though the developers tried to make the "coolness" theme fit into the world of <i>Resident Evil</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Mikami felt it strayed too far from the series' <a href="/wiki/Survival_horror" title="Survival horror">survival horror</a> roots and gradually convinced all of the staff members to make the game independent from it. Kamiya eventually rewrote the story to be set in a world full of demons and changed the hero's name to <a href="/wiki/Dante_(Devil_May_Cry)" title="Dante (Devil May Cry)">Dante</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dmcscenario_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-dmcscenario-28">[28]</a></sup> The cast of characters remained largely identical to that in Sugimura's scenario,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> although the hero's mother<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> and his father,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> the latter an early version of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umbrella_Corporation" title="Umbrella Corporation">Umbrella Corporation</a> founder Lord <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ozwell_E._Spencer" title="Ozwell E. Spencer">Ozwell E. Spencer</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> were written out of the story. The game's new title was revealed as <i><a href="/wiki/Devil_May_Cry_(video_game)" title="Devil May Cry (video game)">Devil May Cry</a></i>, released for the PlayStation 2 in August 2001,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> resulting in <a href="/wiki/Devil_May_Cry" title="Devil May Cry">its own franchise</a>.</p>
<p>Development on <i>Resident Evil 4</i> started over at the end of 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fogbegin_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-fogbegin-41">[41]</a></sup> The first official announcement of the game was made in November 2002, as one of <a href="/wiki/Capcom_Five" title="Capcom Five">five games</a> exclusively developed for the <a href="/wiki/GameCube" title="GameCube">GameCube</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capcom_Production_Studio_4" title="Capcom Production Studio 4">Capcom Production Studio 4</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-productionstudio4_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-productionstudio4-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> This revision, commonly dubbed the "fog version", was directed by Hiroshi Shibata<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jp_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-jp-44">[44]</a></sup> and was 40 percent finished at that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The game saw Leon S. Kennedy desperately struggling to survive<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jp_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-jp-44">[44]</a></sup> after having infiltrated the castle-like Umbrella's main headquarters located in Europe and featured traditional <i>Resident Evil</i> monsters such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zombie_(fictional)" title="Zombie (fictional)">zombies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egm2005_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-egm2005-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespykobayashi_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-gamespykobayashi-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> During the course of the new story which was again written by Sugimura's scenario creation company <a href="/wiki/Flagship_(company)" title="Flagship (company)">Flagship</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Leon became infected with the Progenitor Virus and possessed a hidden power in his left hand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egm2005_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-egm2005-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The producer of the final version also pointed out that Ashley did not appear back then, though there was a different girl who was never revealed to the public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egm2005_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-egm2005-26">[26]</a></sup> The game was to feature some <a href="/wiki/First-person_(video_games)" title="First-person (video games)">first-person</a> perspective gameplay elements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Re3.5hookman.png"><img alt="An image of a young man aiming his gun and flashlight at a hostile male figure wielding a large hook. The whole scene is marked by a bluish hue, giving the mansion environment an otherworldly feel." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="358" data-file-width="512" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bc/Re3.5hookman.png/220px-Re3.5hookman.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bc/Re3.5hookman.png/330px-Re3.5hookman.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bc/Re3.5hookman.png/440px-Re3.5hookman.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Re3.5hookman.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
This screenshot of a canceled version depicts Leon fighting the hook man. Though this earlier revision still used fixed camera angles while exploring environments, the battles already employed the over-the-shoulder view seen in the final build.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Electronic_Entertainment_Expo" title="History of the Electronic Entertainment Expo">E3 2003</a>, another revision was revealed that is widely known as the "hook man version" now,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hookman_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-hookman-52">[52]</a></sup> though officially titled <i>Maboroshi no Biohazard 4</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja" xml:lang="ja">幻の「バイオハザード4」</span><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>, lit. "The Phantom Biohazard 4")</span> on the <i>Biohazard 4 Secret DVD</i>. During Mikami's introduction of the trailer, he assured that development was proceeding very smoothly and claimed the game to be scarier than ever before, warning gamers with the quote "Don't pee your pants!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hookman_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-hookman-52">[52]</a></sup> The story was set in a haunted building where Leon contracted a bizarre disease and fought <a href="/wiki/Paranormal" title="Paranormal">paranormal</a> enemies, such as animated <a href="/wiki/Plate_armour" title="Plate armour">suits of armor</a>, living dolls, and a ghostlike man armed with a large hook.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespykobayashi_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-gamespykobayashi-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hookman_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-hookman-52">[52]</a></sup> The game had an otherworldly feel to it, containing elements like flashbacks and hallucinations that were marked by a bluish tint and a shaking camera.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egm2005_26-4"><a href="#cite_note-egm2005-26">[26]</a></sup> It also displayed various gameplay mechanics that carried over to the final release, like the over-the-shoulder camera and a laser sight for aiming in battles and quick time events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hookman_52-3"><a href="#cite_note-hookman-52">[52]</a></sup> Other features, such as <a href="/wiki/Dialog_tree" title="Dialog tree">dialogue choices</a>, were removed later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egm2005_26-5"><a href="#cite_note-egm2005-26">[26]</a></sup> Though ultimately scrapped, five minutes of gameplay footage for this version was released on the <i>Biohazard 4 Secret DVD</i>, a Japanese <a href="/wiki/Pre-order" title="Pre-order">pre-order</a> bonus given out in January 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Hallucination version had only a basic story concept, having dropped the previous scenario penned by Noboru Sugimura of Flagship. In 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/Resident_Evil_3:_Nemesis" title="Resident Evil 3: Nemesis">Resident Evil 3: Nemesis</a></i> scenario writer Yasuhisa Kawamura said he was responsible for this version, as he wanted to make <i>Biohazard 4</i> scarier "and suggested using a particular scene from the film <i><a href="/wiki/Lost_Souls_(film)" title="Lost Souls (film)">Lost Souls</a></i>, where the main character [...] suddenly finds herself in a derelict building with a killer on the loose. An arranged version of this idea eventually turned into Hook Man. The idea went through several iterations as Mr. Sugimura and I carefully refined this world (which, I have to say, was very romantic). Leon infiltrates the castle of Spencer seeking the truth, while inside a laboratory located deep within, a young girl wakes up. Accompanied by a B.O.W. [an abbreviation for "Bio Organic Weapon" in the series' lore] dog, the two start to make their way up the castle. Unfortunately, there were many obstacles that needed to be overcome and the cost of development was deemed too expensive." Kawamura added he was very sorry and "even ashamed" that Mikami had to step in and scrap this version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> After this attempt, the last canceled revision featured classic zombies again. However, it was discontinued after few months, and before it was ever shown to the public, as the developers felt it was too formulaic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egm2005_26-6"><a href="#cite_note-egm2005-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The story of the Progenitor Virus was eventually covered in <i><a href="/wiki/Resident_Evil_5" title="Resident Evil 5">Resident Evil 5</a></i> and the Spencer Estate became the setting for <i>Resident Evil 5</i> <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_content" title="Downloadable content">downloadable content</a> (DLC) pack "Lost in Nightmares" (featuring Chris Redfield and <a href="/wiki/Jill_Valentine" title="Jill Valentine">Jill Valentine</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_version">Final version</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_Evil_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Final version">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following that, it was decided to reinvent the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespykobayashi_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-gamespykobayashi-46">[46]</a></sup> Mikami took over directorial duties from Shibata and began working on the version that was released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ignkobayashi_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-ignkobayashi-56">[56]</a></sup> In an interview with Game Informer, Mikami explained his decision to shift to a new gameplay system is due to the feeling that the older system is "more of the same" after playing Resident Evil 0. He says that he only felt nervous once more when playing with the newer system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Speaking for the team, game producer Hiroyuki Kobayashi <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ignkobayashi_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-ignkobayashi-56">[56]</a></sup> mentioned how the staff was "tired of the same thing" <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> and how some got bored and moved on to other projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> In addition to that, the producer also felt that the older format was "stuck in a cookie cutter mold" and described it as "shackles holding us down".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, despite what Kobayashi said, not every single staff member was on the same page about changing the gameplay system. Kobayashi mentioned how some of the development team felt depressed and were hard to motivate after the focus of the game shifted from horror to action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fogbegin_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-fogbegin-41">[41]</a></sup> Although Mikami demanded the camera system to be completely revised, the staff members had reservations about making big changes to the series he had created.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendopowerkobayashi_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-nintendopowerkobayashi-61">[61]</a></sup> Eventually, he intervened, explained his proposed changes, and wrote a new story for the title that, unlike previous installments, was not centered on the company Umbrella.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendopowerkobayashi_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-nintendopowerkobayashi-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-staffjp_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-staffjp-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ignint_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-ignint-63">[63]</a></sup> Inspired by <i><a href="/wiki/Onimusha_3:_Demon_Siege" title="Onimusha 3: Demon Siege">Onimusha 3: Demon Siege</a></i>, a game Mikami had enjoyed playing but felt could have been better with a different view, he decided to place the camera behind the playable character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> To go along with the new gameplay and story, a new type of enemy called "Ganado" was created, as opposed to using the undead creatures from previous <i>Resident Evil</i> games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ignint_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-ignint-63">[63]</a></sup> Furthermore, producers expended additional detail to modify and update characters that had previously appeared in the series. In a documentary explaining the conception of the game's characters, Kamiya stated he intended to make Leon Kennedy "look tougher, but also cool".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dvd_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-dvd-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>The game's English <a href="/wiki/Voice_acting" title="Voice acting">voice actors</a> recorded their parts in four sessions, over three to four months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cary_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-cary-66">[66]</a></sup> Capcom assigned Shinsaku Ohara as the game's script translator and voice over coordinator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-credits_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-credits-67">[67]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carolyn_Lawrence" title="Carolyn Lawrence">Carolyn Lawrence</a>, who provided the voice for Ashley Graham, described her character as "vulnerable, because Leon has to come to her rescue all the time".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cary_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-cary-66">[66]</a></sup> She also described Kennedy's character as "more brawn, perhaps, than brain".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cary_66-2"><a href="#cite_note-cary-66">[66]</a></sup> In addition to the voice acting, the game's designer detailed each cinematic sequence so that each character's facial expressions matched the tone of their voice actor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dvd_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-dvd-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Along with <i><a href="/wiki/Resident_Evil:_Dead_Aim" title="Resident Evil: Dead Aim">Resident Evil: Dead Aim</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Resident_Evil_Outbreak" title="Resident Evil Outbreak">Resident Evil Outbreak</a></i>, two side story titles that did not fall under the exclusive policy, it was announced on October 31, 2004 that <i>Resident Evil 4</i> would come to the PlayStation 2 in 2005, citing increased profit, changing market conditions, and increased consumer satisfaction as the key reasons. The PlayStation 2 version included new features, primarily a new sub game featuring Ada Wong. On February 1, 2006, <a href="/wiki/Ubisoft" title="Ubisoft">Ubisoft</a> announced that they would be publishing the game on the PC for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> On April 4, 2007, a <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> version was announced and was launched later in the year. The game features all of the extras in the PS2 version, along with other additions, including a trailer for <i><a href="/wiki/Resident_Evil:_The_Umbrella_Chronicles" title="Resident Evil: The Umbrella Chronicles">Resident Evil: The Umbrella Chronicles</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-joystiqwii_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-joystiqwii-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cubed3wii_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-cubed3wii-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_Evil_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The original version for the GameCube featured two different collector's editions of the game. The first was available as a pre-order that included the game, <i>Prologue</i> art book, and a T-shirt. <a href="/wiki/GameStop" title="GameStop">GameStop</a> offered another limited edition that was packaged in a tin box with the art book, a <a href="/wiki/Cel" title="Cel">cel</a> of Leon, and a soundtrack CD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Australia received an exclusive collector's edition that came with the game and a bonus disc with interviews and creator's footage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ports">Ports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_Evil_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Resident Evil 4</i> was ported to the PlayStation 2 after Capcom stated that it did not fall under the exclusivity deal with <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a>. It was released in North America on October 25, 2005. The largest addition to the game is "Separate Ways", a new scenario for Ada written by Haruo Murata.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-credits_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-credits-67">[67]</a></sup> According to producer Masachika Kawata, the Separate Ways campaign was something thought up by the PS2 porting team and was added after getting approval from Shinji Mikami.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The port was later included with <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resident_Evil_Code:_Veronica#Re-releases" title="Resident Evil Code: Veronica">Resident Evil Code: Veronica X</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Resident_Evil_Outbreak" title="Resident Evil Outbreak">Resident Evil Outbreak</a></i> as part of the compilation <i>Resident Evil: The Essentials</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The PlayStation 2 version featured two standard and collector's bundles from pre-orders. The standard package included the game and a T-shirt, while the collector's bundle included the game, a T-shirt, a figurine of Leon, and the soundtrack <i>Biohazard Sound Chronicle Best Track Box</i>. This quickly sold out, and a second pressing was released that included an Ada figurine. Another, called the <i>Resident Evil 4: Premium Edition</i>, was packaged in a SteelBook media case, along with the art book, a documentary DVD, and a cel art of Ada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>A PC port of <i>Resident Evil 4</i> developed by Sourcenext was first released in Hong Kong on February 1, 2007, published by <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Games" title="Typhoon Games">Typhoon Games</a>. It was later released in Europe, North America, and Australia in March 2007 and was published by <a href="/wiki/Ubisoft" title="Ubisoft">Ubisoft</a>. The port contains the bonus features from the PS2 version, such as "Separate Ways", the P.R.L. 412 laser cannon and a second set of unlockable costumes for Leon and Ashley, as well as an Easy difficulty level. It also supports multiple widescreen resolutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The shadow and lighting issues were fixed in the first and the only patch for the game, Version 1.10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-re4pcpatch_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-re4pcpatch-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><b>Resident Evil 4: Wii Edition</b></i> was released for the <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> on May 31, 2007 in Japan and on June 19, 2007 in the United States. It features updated controls that utilize the <a href="/wiki/Pointing_device" title="Pointing device">pointing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Motion_controller" title="Motion controller">motion-sensing</a> abilities of the <a href="/wiki/Wii_Remote" title="Wii Remote">Wii Remote</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wii_Nunchuk" title="Wii Nunchuk">Nunchuk</a>, though both the GameCube controller and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Super_Famicom_Classic_Controller" title="Super Famicom Classic Controller">Classic Controller</a> are also supported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cubed3wii_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-cubed3wii-70">[70]</a></sup> The Wii Remote is able to aim and shoot anywhere on the screen with a <a href="/wiki/Reticle" title="Reticle">reticle</a> that replaces the laser sight found in the other versions, and motion-based gestures are used to perform some context-sensitive actions, such as dodging or slashing Leon's knife. The <i>Wii Edition</i> also includes the extra content from the PS2 and PC versions, and a trailer for <i><a href="/wiki/Resident_Evil:_The_Umbrella_Chronicles" title="Resident Evil: The Umbrella Chronicles">Resident Evil: The Umbrella Chronicles</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-joystiqwii_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-joystiqwii-69">[69]</a></sup> The <i>Wii Edition</i> became available for <a href="/wiki/Digital_distribution" title="Digital distribution">download</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_eShop" title="Nintendo eShop">Nintendo eShop</a> in Europe on October 29, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref--DigitalSpyWiiEdition-eShop_78-0"><a href="#cite_note--DigitalSpyWiiEdition-eShop-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NinLife-Oct29-Nintendo-eShop_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-NinLife-Oct29-Nintendo-eShop-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><b>Resident Evil 4: Mobile Edition</b></i> was released in Japan for <a href="/wiki/Au_(mobile_phone_company)" title="Au (mobile phone company)">au</a>'s BREW 4.0 on February 1, 2008. It was first announced by Capcom at TGS 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Differences from the original include changing the flow of the story from being continuous to being divided into sections such as "Village", "Ravene", "Fortress" and "Subterranean Tunnel". There is also a more challenging Mercenary Mode.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The game uses the MascotCapsule eruption engine<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> and was adapted to the <a href="/wiki/Zeebo" title="Zeebo">Zeebo</a> and <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> platforms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-res4ios_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-res4ios-85">[85]</a></sup> On July 13, 2009, without any formal announcement, <i>Resident Evil 4: Mobile Edition</i> was released by Capcom for the iOS platform via the <a href="/wiki/App_Store_(iOS)" title="App Store (iOS)">App Store</a> in Japan, but was quickly removed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> though some players were able to purchase and download the game. The game has since been officially released in Japan and North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-res4ios_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-res4ios-85">[85]</a></sup> Later, Capcom made an update that had different difficulty levels and high scores. Recently, Capcom released a new separate version called <i>Resident Evil 4 for Beginners</i>, which offers the first two levels (three counting a training level) of both Story Mode and Mercenary Mode. However, the rest of the levels are available for purchase in-game as downloadable content. Due to the release of the <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPad</a>, Capcom recreated the iPhone version of <i>Resident Evil 4: Mobile Edition</i> and updated it to HD graphics as <i><b>Resident Evil 4: iPad Edition</b></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 23, 2011, <a href="/wiki/High-definition_video" title="High-definition video">high-definition</a> remastered versions of both <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resident_Evil_Code:_Veronica" title="Resident Evil Code: Veronica">Resident Evil Code: Veronica</a></i> and <i>Resident Evil 4</i> were announced to be in development for the <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a> and <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>, as part of the <i>Resident Evil: Revival Selection</i> series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The ports are to feature all the bonus content from the previous releases, including "Separate Ways". On July 23, 2011 Capcom announced at Comic-Con 2011 that Resident Evil 4 would be released on September 20, 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Network" title="PlayStation Network">PlayStation Network</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xbox_Live_Marketplace#Xbox_Live_Games_on_Demand" title="Xbox Live Marketplace">Xbox Live Games on Demand</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> In Japan, <i>Resident Evil 4</i> and <i>Resident Evil Code: Veronica</i> were released on a single disc with the title <i>Biohazard Revival Selection</i> on September 8, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> For North America and Europe, both titles, including <i><b>Resident Evil 4 HD</b></i>, were only released as downloads on Xbox Live Games on Demand and PlayStation Network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> On February 27, 2014, Capcom released <i><b>Resident Evil 4 Ultimate HD Edition</b></i> for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>. The port features improved graphics and many other enhancements that were included in <i>Resident Evil 4 HD</i>. <i>Resident Evil 4</i> was re-released on <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a> on August 30, 2016.</p>
<p>In April 2013, <i>Resident Evil 4</i> was released on <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>, but outside of Japan, it is exclusive to <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a> through <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_Apps" title="Samsung Galaxy Apps">Samsung Galaxy Apps</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Merchandise">Merchandise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_Evil_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Merchandise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An album titled <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biohazard_4_Original_Soundtrack" title="Biohazard 4 Original Soundtrack">Biohazard 4 Original Soundtrack</a></i> was released in Japan on December 22, 2005. It contains 62 compositions from the game and the 48-page <i>Visual Booklet</i> with liner notes from composers Shusaku Uchiyama and Misao Senbongi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Other merchandise for the game included figures by <a href="/wiki/McFarlane_Toys" title="McFarlane Toys">McFarlane Toys</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/National_Entertainment_Collectibles_Association" title="National Entertainment Collectibles Association">NECA</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Hot_Toys" title="Hot Toys">Hot Toys</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Agatsuma_Entertainment" title="Agatsuma Entertainment">Agatsuma Entertainment</a> has also created various miniature collectibles based on several main characters and enemies from <i>Resident Evil 4</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Two special controllers designed to resemble chainsaws were designed by NubyTech for use with the game's GameCube and PlayStation 2 versions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_Evil_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales">Sales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_Evil_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Sales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The GameCube version sold over 320,000 copies in North America during the first twenty days. The European release sold its entire 200,000 copies during the first month. By January 2006, over 3,000,000 copies of the GameCube and PlayStation 2 versions had been shipped worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> According to January 17, 2007 sales figures provided by Capcom, the GameCube version of <i>Resident Evil 4</i> has sold a total of 1.6 million copies worldwide, while the PS2 version has sold over 2 million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> As of September 30, 2011, the PS2 version has sold 2.2 million copies and the <i>Wii Edition</i> has sold 1.9 million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> According to Capcom's Platinum Titles list, the game has sold 5.9 million copies across all formats, making it the fourth biggest-selling <i>Resident Evil</i> title and for which it holds the record for "Best-Selling Survival Horror Game" in the 2012 <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records_Gamer%27s_Edition" title="Guinness World Records Gamer's Edition">Guinness World Records Gamer's Edition</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> In addition, the 2014 Windows release of <i>Ultimate HD Edition</i> sold more than 650,000 copies on <a href="/wiki/Steam_(software)" title="Steam (software)">Steam</a> as of December 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>

<p><i>Resident Evil 4</i> was critically acclaimed and received an overall score of 96/100 on <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a> for the GameCube and PlayStation 2 versions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MC_NGC_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-MC_NGC-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MC_PS2_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-MC_PS2-131">[131]</a></sup> In addition to the gameplay, the characters and story generally received positive commentary, leading to the finished product being deemed by most as <a href="/wiki/List_of_video_games_considered_the_best" title="List of video games considered the best">one of the best video games ever made</a>. <a href="/wiki/GameSpot" title="GameSpot">GameSpot</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Greg_Kasavin" title="Greg Kasavin">Greg Kasavin</a> praised the game's voice acting, but claimed that it was betrayed by "some uncharacteristically goofy dialogue".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespotgc_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-gamespotgc-111">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Games" title="Yahoo! Games">Yahoo! Games</a>' Adam Pavlacka and GameSpot's Kevin VanOrd acclaimed Capcom for adding great amounts of detail to the game's characters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespotwii_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-gamespotwii-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matt_Casamassina" title="Matt Casamassina">Matt Casamassina</a> went into further detail in his review for <i>Resident Evil 4</i>, praising not only the detailed character design but also the <a href="/wiki/Stage_combat" title="Stage combat">fight choreography</a> and three-dimensional modeling within cinematic sequences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-ign-119">[119]</a></sup> Casamassina also complimented the game's voice actors, especially <a href="/wiki/Paul_Mercier_(actor)" title="Paul Mercier (actor)">Paul Mercier</a> (Leon), commenting, "For once, the characters are believable because Capcom has hired competent actors to supply their voices. Leon in particular is very well produced".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-ign-119">[119]</a></sup> IGN and <i><a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Power" title="Nintendo Power">Nintendo Power</a></i> specifically recognized <i>Resident Evil 4</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s character design and voice acting. The increased variety of weapons has been praised by gaming publications such as <i><a href="/wiki/GamePro" title="GamePro">GamePro</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> and Game Over Online.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Review_of_Resident_Evil_4_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Review_of_Resident_Evil_4-136">[136]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/G4_(U.S._TV_channel)" title="G4 (U.S. TV channel)">G4</a> TV show <a href="/wiki/X-Play" title="X-Play">X-Play</a> gave it a 5 out of 5, for introducing a new style of gameplay for the series as well as incorporating moments where the player would have to interact with the cut scenes. Not long after, it was awarded as the best game ever reviewed on the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> The makers of <i>Resident Evil 4</i> worked on various innovations associated with the use and inventory of weapons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Game Over stated that players can use the vast array of weapons to "go for headshots now".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Review_of_Resident_Evil_4_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-Review_of_Resident_Evil_4-136">[136]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Game_Informer" title="Game Informer">Game Informer</a></i> stated that ammunition is more plentiful in <i>Resident Evil 4</i> than in other games in the series, making the game more action-oriented.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ratings of the PC port were not as high as for the other versions. It was heavily criticized for no <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mouse_(computing)" title="Mouse (computing)">mouse</a> support and frustrating keyboard controls, low-quality <a href="/wiki/Full_motion_video" title="Full motion video">FMV</a> <a href="/wiki/Cutscene" title="Cutscene">cut scenes</a>, choppy graphics rendering (lacks shadows and proper lighting) and requiring a gamepad controller for more precise aiming and gameplay. Despite the issues, the game still received generally positive reviews from IGN and GameSpot that praised the gameplay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespotpc_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-gamespotpc-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ignpc_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-ignpc-120">[120]</a></sup> Japanese game magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Famitsu" title="Famitsu">Famitsu</a></i> reviewed the Wii version of the game, with two editors giving the game a perfect 10 score, and the remaining pair giving it a 9, resulting in a score of 38 out of 40. The reviewers noted that the game's improved controls offer something fresh and different. Multiple reviewers agreed that even those who own the original will find something fun and enjoyable in this version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ignfamitsu_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-ignfamitsu-110">[110]</a></sup> British magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Gamer" title="Nintendo Gamer">NGamer</a></i> gave the <i>Wii Edition</i> a score of 96%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MC_Wii_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-MC_Wii-1">[1]</a></sup> slightly lower than the 97% given to the GameCube version. They praised the visuals, controls, and features and commented on the fact that such an "exceptional package" was on sale for a low price; however, when writing about the Wii controls, they said, "if you've played the GC version this won't be as special". <i><a href="/wiki/Official_Nintendo_Magazine" title="Official Nintendo Magazine">Official Nintendo Magazine</a></i> gave the Wii version 94%, 3% less than the original due to it simply not having the same impact it did back then.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ONMwii_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-ONMwii-140">[140]</a></sup> IGN praised the Wii version, stating it is the superior edition, but does not push the Wii like it did with GameCube and PS2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN_Wii_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-IGN_Wii-3">[3]</a></sup> GameSpot praised the new controls of the <i>Wii Edition</i> but commented on the lack of exclusive Wii features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespotwii_114-2"><a href="#cite_note-gamespotwii-114">[114]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Hyper_(magazine)" title="Hyper (magazine)">Hyper</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Jonti Davies commended <i>Resident Evil 4: Wii Edition</i> for its "visual improvements" but criticized it for having "no new content".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> The PS3 version of <i>Resident Evil 4 HD</i> received a score of 9.0 from <a href="/wiki/Destructoid" title="Destructoid">Destructoid</a>, which called it "a hallmark of excellence".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>In their October 2013 issue, <i><a href="/wiki/Edge_(magazine)" title="Edge (magazine)">Edge</a></i> retroactively awarded the game ten out of ten, one of twenty-three games to achieve that perfect score in the magazine's twenty-year history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edgeten_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-edgeten-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_Evil_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The game has received several awards from various organizations from various video game websites. It was named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_of_the_Year" title="Game of the Year">Game of the Year</a> at the 2005 <i><a href="/wiki/Spike_Video_Game_Awards" title="Spike Video Game Awards">Spike Video Game Awards</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Power" title="Nintendo Power">Nintendo Power</a></i> also named it their 2005 Game of the Year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendopower_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-nintendopower-123">[123]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Game_Informer" title="Game Informer">Game Informer</a></i> named it their 2005 Game of the Year as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gameinformer_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-gameinformer-144">[144]</a></sup> It tied with <i><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_Hearts_II" title="Kingdom Hearts II">Kingdom Hearts II</a></i> as <i><a href="/wiki/Famitsu" title="Famitsu">Famitsu</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Game of the Year 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> <i>Nintendo Power</i> acknowledged the title's voice acting in its 2005 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nintendo_Power_Awards" title="Nintendo Power Awards">Nintendo Power Awards</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> gave the game the "Best Artistic Design" award in its "Best of 2005" segment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Game_Developers_Association" title="International Game Developers Association">International Game Developers Association</a> nominated <i>Resident Evil 4</i> for their best "Visual Arts" award,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> but lost the award to <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Shadow_of_the_Colossus" title="Shadow of the Colossus">Shadow of the Colossus</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Resident Evil 4</i> is often considered one of the best video games of all time. <i>Nintendo Power</i> ranked it as number one top best GameCube games of all time" in 2005<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendopower_123-2"><a href="#cite_note-nintendopower-123">[123]</a></sup> and also ranked it second on their list of the best games of the 2000s in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> In 2008, <i>Resident Evil 4</i> was also ranked first place in the list of the best video games of all time according to the readers of IGN.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> In 2009, <i>Game Informer</i> ranked <i>Resident Evil 4</i> number one on their list of top GameCube games<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> and number three on their list of top PlayStation 2 games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ScrewAttack" title="ScrewAttack">ScrewAttack</a> named <i>Resident Evil 4</i> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ScrewAttack%27s_Top_10" title="ScrewAttack's Top 10">best GameCube game of all time</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> while <i>GamePro</i> ranked it as the second best game for the PS2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> In 2010, the readers of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PlayStation_Official_Magazine_-_UK" title="PlayStation Official Magazine - UK">PlayStation Official Magazine</a></i> voted it the 10th greatest <a href="/wiki/PlayStation" title="PlayStation">PlayStation</a> title ever released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> In 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/Edge_(magazine)" title="Edge (magazine)">Edge</a></i> ranked the game at second place in its list of top games of all time, behind only <i><a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_Zelda:_Ocarina_of_Time" title="The Legend of Zelda: Ocarina of Time">The Legend of Zelda: Ocarina of Time</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> That same year, <a href="/wiki/G4_(U.S._TV_channel)" title="G4 (U.S. TV channel)">G4</a> named it the 21st top video game of all time, calling it "a modern horror masterpiece."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> In 2015, the game placed 7th on USgamer's The 15 Best Games Since 2000 list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> In early 2006, in their 200th issue, <i>Nintendo Power</i> ranked it in second place in their Top 200 Games of all-time list, also behind only <i>The Legend of Zelda: Ocarina of Time</i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_Evil_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Resident Evil 4</i> is regarded as one of the most influential games of the <a href="/wiki/2000s_in_video_gaming" title="2000s in video gaming">2000s decade</a>, due to its influence in redefining the <a href="/wiki/Third-person_shooter" title="Third-person shooter">third-person shooter</a> genre<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nationalpost_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-nationalpost-160">[160]</a></sup> by introducing a "reliance on offset camera angles that fail to obscure the action".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> The new gameplay alterations and immersive style appealed to many not previously familiar with the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> The over-the-shoulder viewpoint introduced in <i>Resident Evil 4</i> has later become standard in third-person shooters, including titles ranging from <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gears_of_War_(series)" title="Gears of War (series)">Gears of War</a></i> to <i><a href="/wiki/Batman:_Arkham_Asylum" title="Batman: Arkham Asylum">Batman: Arkham Asylum</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nationalpost_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-nationalpost-160">[160]</a></sup> It has also become a standard "precision aim" feature for <a href="/wiki/Action_game" title="Action game">action games</a> in general, with examples ranging from <i><a href="/wiki/Dead_Space_(series)" title="Dead Space (series)">Dead Space</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto" title="Grand Theft Auto">Grand Theft Auto</a></i> to the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ratchet_%26_Clank_Future" title="Ratchet &amp; Clank Future">Ratchet &amp; Clank Future</a></i> series and <i><a href="/wiki/Fallout_(series)" title="Fallout (series)">Fallout</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Resident Evil 4</i> redefined the survival horror genre by emphasizing reflexes and precision aiming,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> thus broadening the gameplay of the series with elements from the wider action game genre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> However, this also led some reviewers to suggest that the <i>Resident Evil</i> series had abandoned the survival horror genre,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-extinction_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-extinction-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> by demolishing the genre conventions that it had established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fear101_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-fear101-168">[168]</a></sup> Other major survival horror series followed suit, by developing their combat systems to feature more action, such as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silent_Hill_Homecoming" title="Silent Hill Homecoming">Silent Hill Homecoming</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-extinction_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-extinction-166">[166]</a></sup> and the 2008 version of <i><a href="/wiki/Alone_in_the_Dark_(2008_video_game)" title="Alone in the Dark (2008 video game)">Alone in the Dark</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> These changes represent an overall trend among <a href="/wiki/Console_game" title="Console game">console games</a> shifting towards visceral action gameplay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leigh_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-leigh-170">[170]</a></sup> While working on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_of_Us" title="The Last of Us">The Last of Us</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Naughty_Dog" title="Naughty Dog">Naughty Dog</a> took cues from <i>Resident Evil 4</i>, particularly the tension and action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Resident_Evil_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-fogbegin-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-fogbegin_41-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fogbegin_41-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">"Resident Evil 4 Entwickler-Tagebuch – Teil 1: Die Entstehung". <i>N-Zone</i> (in German). [...] Hiroyuki Kobayashi: Es war nicht einfach, das Team bei Laune zu halten, nachdem wir die Richtung des Spiels so radikal verändert hatten. Als die Entscheidung getroffen wurde, das Spiel actionlastiger zu gestalten, war die Stimmung im Team schon sehr gedrückt. / The first work on <i>Resident Evil 4</i> already begun at the end of 2001. The size of team varies depending on the stage of development, about 60 people are working on the title at the moment. [...] Hiroyuki Kobayashi: It was not easy to keep the team going after we changed the direction of the game so radically. When it was decided to make the game more action-oriented, the team felt really depressed.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AResident+Evil+4&amp;rft.atitle=Resident+Evil+4+Entwickler-Tagebuch+%93+Teil+1%3A+Die+Entstehung&amp;rft.date=2004-12&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.issue=12%2F2004&amp;rft.jtitle=N-Zone&amp;rft.pages=76-77&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-nintendopowerkobayashi-61"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-nintendopowerkobayashi_61-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nintendopowerkobayashi_61-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">"New Evil". <i>Nintendo Power</i>. Nintendo of America, Inc. (180). June 2004. <q>The Umbrella Corporation is no more. "It's the only thing that makes sense, if you think about it," explains Resident Evil 4 producer Hiroyuki Kobayshi. "Why would the U.S. government allow a company that developed the T-virus, and in the end forced them to destroy an entire city, to continue to exist? They wouldn't. Hence the rationale for Umbrella going away after RE3." [...] "Right from the start, we wanted to do something new and innovative for the series, so Mikami issued an order to the team: 'I want to totally re-create how the polygons, the camera, everything looks.' But, every time the staff tried to do it without his direction, they only came out with little minor changes. Nothing major. Perhaps they were too afraid to take this series that he created and totally change it. But anyway, he stepped in and showed what he wanted."</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AResident+Evil+4&amp;rft.atitle=New+Evil&amp;rft.date=2004-06&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.issue=180&amp;rft.jtitle=Nintendo+Power&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
